## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ordinary differential rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an instantaneous reaction rate expressed as a time-derivative of concentration A, which is the core object of chemical kinetics. With available variables (t, A), the most likely structures are ODE rate laws where the rate depends on A (reaction order, autocatalysis, inhibition) and possibly explicit time-dependence via time-varying rate coefficients or forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate process, e.g., saturated surface reaction)
- First-order decay/growth: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular kinetics; sign of c0 sets growth vs decay)
- General power-law (n-th order): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical/elementary reaction order fit)
- Second-order (bimolecular in A): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (e.g., 2A -> products)
- Mixed source + first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (inflow/outgassing plus unimolecular loss)
- Quadratic polynomial rate: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (effective kinetics from lumped mechanisms)
- Reversible first-order toward equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Logistic-type autocatalysis with carrying limit: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplifying growth with depletion/finite capacity)
- Cubic/quenching term: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**3 (growth with nonlinear self-limitation, effective radical recombination)
- Rational saturation/inhibition (effective rate law): dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate limited at high A by saturation/complexation)
- Rational with substrate inhibition-like shape: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (rise then fall at high A due to inhibition/side-pathway)
- Time-varying first-order coefficient: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (rate constant drift due to heating, aging, or catalyst deactivation trends)
- Exponentially varying first-order coefficient: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (activation/deactivation causing k(t) to change exponentially)
- Periodic forcing of rate coefficient: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (modulated kinetics under periodic irradiation/mixing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt depends only on A (no explicit t), the mechanism is time-homogeneous; explicit t terms suggest changing conditions (k(t)) or external forcing.
- Near-equilibrium relaxation often appears as a linear restoring form c*(A_eq âˆ’ A), giving approximately exponential return to A_eq when integrated.
- Reaction order can be inferred from how dA_dt scales with A: proportional to A (first order), A**2 (second order), or A**n (general).
- Autocatalysis typically produces a factor A multiplied by a depletion term (c âˆ’ A) or other nonlinearities, yielding sigmoidal A(t) upon integration.
- High-concentration saturation or inhibition is often captured by rational forms where increases in A yield diminishing increments in dA_dt, or even downturn at large A.
- Presence of both constant and A-dependent terms suggests parallel pathways (e.g., background source plus reaction loss).
- Odd-power damping terms (e.g., âˆ’A**3) often represent effective recombination/quenching or nonlinear stabilization in lumped radical models.
- Periodic dependence on t (sin/cos) is a hallmark of externally modulated kinetics (light chopping, pulsed feed, oscillatory reactor conditions).
